900  } 901  } 902  } 903  } 904  905  /** 906  * Releases a list of object IDs. For each object in the list, the 907  * following applies. 908  * The count of references held by the back-end (the reference 909  * count) will be decremented by refCnt. 910  * If thereafter the reference count is less than 911  * or equal to zero, the ID is freed. 912  * Any back-end resources associated with the freed ID may 913  * be freed, and if garbage collection was 914  * disabled for the object, it will be re-enabled. 915  * The sender of this command 916  * promises that no further commands will be sent 917  * referencing a freed ID. 918  * <p> 919  * Use of this command is not required. If it is not sent, 920  * resources associated with each ID will be freed by the back-end 921  * at some time after the corresponding object is garbage collected. 922  * It is most useful to use this command to reduce the load on the 923  * back-end if a very large number of 924  * objects has been retrieved from the back-end (a large array, 925  * for example) but may not be garbage collected any time soon. 926  * <p> 927  * IDs may be re-used by the back-end after they 928  * have been freed with this command. 929  * This description assumes reference counting, 930  * a back-end may use any implementation which operates 931  * equivalently. 932  */ 933  static class DisposeObjects { 934  static final int COMMAND = 14; 935  936  static class Request { 937  938  /** 939  * The object ID 940  */ 941  final ObjectReferenceImpl object; 942  943  /** 944  * The number of times this object ID has been 945  * part of a packet received from the back-end. 946  * An accurate count prevents the object ID 947  * from being freed on the back-end if 948  * it is part of an incoming packet, not yet 949  * handled by the front-end. 950  */ 951  final int refCnt; 952  953  Request(ObjectReferenceImpl object, int refCnt) { 954  this.object = object; 955  this.refCnt = refCnt; 956  } 957  958  private void write(PacketStream ps) { 959  if ((ps.vm.traceFlags & VirtualMachineImpl.TRACE_SENDS) != 0) { 960  ps.vm.printTrace("Sending: object(ObjectReferenceImpl): " + (object==null?"NULL":"ref="+object.ref())); 961  } 962  ps.writeObjectRef(object.ref()); 963  if ((ps.vm.traceFlags & VirtualMachineImpl.TRACE_SENDS) != 0) { 964  ps.vm.printTrace("Sending: refCnt(int): " + refCnt); 965  } 966  ps.writeInt(refCnt); 967  } 968  } 969  970  static DisposeObjects process(VirtualMachineImpl vm, 971  Request[] requests) 972  throws JDWPException { 973  PacketStream ps = enqueueCommand(vm, requests); 974  return waitForReply(vm, ps); 975  } 976  977  static PacketStream enqueueCommand(VirtualMachineImpl vm, 978  Request[] requests) { 979  PacketStream ps = new PacketStream(vm, COMMAND_SET, COMMAND); 980  if ((vm.traceFlags & VirtualMachineImpl.TRACE_SENDS) != 0) { 981  vm.printTrace("Sending Command(id=" + ps.pkt.id + ") JDWP.VirtualMachine.DisposeObjects"+(ps.pkt.flags!=0?", FLAGS=" + ps.pkt.flags:"")); 982  } 983  if ((ps.vm.traceFlags & VirtualMachineImpl.TRACE_SENDS) != 0) { 984  ps.vm.printTrace("Sending: requests(Request[]): " + ""); 985  } 986  ps.writeInt(requests.length); 987  for (int i = 0; i < requests.length; i++) {; 988  if ((ps.vm.traceFlags & VirtualMachineImpl.TRACE_SENDS) != 0) { 989  ps.vm.printTrace("Sending: requests[i](Request): " + ""); 990  } 991  requests[i].write(ps); 992  } 993  ps.send(); 994  return ps; 995  } 996  997  static DisposeObjects waitForReply(VirtualMachineImpl vm, PacketStream ps) 998  throws JDWPException { 999  ps.waitForReply(); 1000  return new DisposeObjects(vm, ps); 1001  } 1002  1003  1004  private DisposeObjects(VirtualMachineImpl vm, PacketStream ps) { 1005  if (vm.traceReceives) { 1006  vm.printTrace("Receiving Command(id=" + ps.pkt.id + ") JDWP.VirtualMachine.DisposeObjects"+(ps.pkt.flags!=0?", FLAGS=" + ps.pkt.flags:"")+(ps.pkt.errorCode!=0?", ERROR CODE=" + ps.pkt.errorCode:"")); 1007  } 1008  } 1009  } 1010  1011  /** 1012  * Tells the target VM to stop sending events. Events are not discarded; 1013  * they are held until a subsequent ReleaseEvents command is sent. 1014  * This command is useful to control the number of events sent 1015  * to the debugger VM in situations where very large numbers of events 1016  * are generated. 1017  * While events are held by the debugger back-end, application 1018  * execution may be frozen by the debugger back-end to prevent 1019  * buffer overflows on the back end. 1020  * Responses to commands are never held and are not affected by this 1021  * command. 3363  } 3364  } 3365  } 3366  3367  /** 3368  * Invokes a static method. 3369  * The method must be member of the class type 3370  * or one of its superclasses. 3371  * Access control is not enforced; for example, private 3372  * methods can be invoked. 3373  * <p> 3374  * The method invocation will occur in the specified thread. 3375  * Method invocation can occur only if the specified thread 3376  * has been suspended by an event. 3377  * Method invocation is not supported 3378  * when the target VM has been suspended by the front-end. 3379  * <p> 3380  * The specified method is invoked with the arguments in the specified 3381  * argument list. 3382  * The method invocation is synchronous; the reply packet is not 3383  * sent until the invoked method returns in the target VM. 3384  * The return value (possibly the void value) is 3385  * included in the reply packet. 3386  * If the invoked method throws an exception, the 3387  * exception object ID is set in the reply packet; otherwise, the 3388  * exception object ID is null. 3389  * <p> 3390  * For primitive arguments, the argument value's type must match the 3391  * argument's type exactly. For object arguments, there must exist a 3392  * widening reference conversion from the argument value's type to the 3393  * argument's type and the argument's type must be loaded. 3394  * <p> 3395  * By default, all threads in the target VM are resumed while 3396  * the method is being invoked if they were previously 3397  * suspended by an event or by command. 3398  * This is done to prevent the deadlocks 3399  * that will occur if any of the threads own monitors 3400  * that will be needed by the invoked method. It is possible that 3401  * breakpoints or other events might occur during the invocation. 3402  * Note, however, that this implicit resume acts exactly like 3403  * the ThreadReference resume command, so if the thread's suspend 3404  * count is greater than 1, it will remain in a suspended state 3405  * during the invocation. By default, when the invocation completes, 3406  * all threads in the target VM are suspended, regardless their state 3407  * before the invocation. 3408  * <p> 3409  * The resumption of other threads during the invoke can be prevented 3410  * by specifying the INVOKE_SINGLE_THREADED 3411  * bit flag in the <code>options</code> field; however, 3412  * there is no protection against or recovery from the deadlocks 3413  * described above, so this option should be used with great caution. 3414  * Only the specified thread will be resumed (as described for all 3415  * threads above). Upon completion of a single threaded invoke, the invoking thread 3416  * will be suspended once again. Note that any threads started during 3417  * the single threaded invocation will not be suspended when the 3418  * invocation completes. 3419  * <p> 3420  * If the target VM is disconnected during the invoke (for example, through 3421  * the VirtualMachine dispose command) the method invocation continues. 3422  */ 3423  static class InvokeMethod { 3424  static final int COMMAND = 3; 3707  } 3708  } 3709  } 3710  } 3711  3712  static class InterfaceType { 3713  static final int COMMAND_SET = 5; 3714  private InterfaceType() {} // hide constructor 3715  3716  /** 3717  * Invokes a static method. 3718  * The method must not be a static initializer. 3719  * The method must be a member of the interface type. 3720  * <p>Since JDWP version 1.8 3721  * <p> 3722  * The method invocation will occur in the specified thread. 3723  * Method invocation can occur only if the specified thread 3724  * has been suspended by an event. 3725  * Method invocation is not supported 3726  * when the target VM has been suspended by the front-end. 3727  * <p> 3728  * The specified method is invoked with the arguments in the specified 3729  * argument list. 3730  * The method invocation is synchronous; the reply packet is not 3731  * sent until the invoked method returns in the target VM. 3732  * The return value (possibly the void value) is 3733  * included in the reply packet. 3734  * If the invoked method throws an exception, the 3735  * exception object ID is set in the reply packet; otherwise, the 3736  * exception object ID is null. 3737  * <p> 3738  * For primitive arguments, the argument value's type must match the 3739  * argument's type exactly. For object arguments, there must exist a 3740  * widening reference conversion from the argument value's type to the 3741  * argument's type and the argument's type must be loaded. 3742  * <p> 3743  * By default, all threads in the target VM are resumed while 3744  * the method is being invoked if they were previously 3745  * suspended by an event or by a command. 3746  * This is done to prevent the deadlocks 3747  * that will occur if any of the threads own monitors 3748  * that will be needed by the invoked method. It is possible that 3749  * breakpoints or other events might occur during the invocation. 3750  * Note, however, that this implicit resume acts exactly like 3751  * the ThreadReference resume command, so if the thread's suspend 3752  * count is greater than 1, it will remain in a suspended state 3753  * during the invocation. By default, when the invocation completes, 3754  * all threads in the target VM are suspended, regardless their state 3755  * before the invocation. 3756  * <p> 3757  * The resumption of other threads during the invoke can be prevented 3758  * by specifying the INVOKE_SINGLE_THREADED 3759  * bit flag in the <code>options</code> field; however, 3760  * there is no protection against or recovery from the deadlocks 3761  * described above, so this option should be used with great caution. 3762  * Only the specified thread will be resumed (as described for all 3763  * threads above). Upon completion of a single threaded invoke, the invoking thread 3764  * will be suspended once again. Note that any threads started during 3765  * the single threaded invocation will not be suspended when the 3766  * invocation completes. 3767  * <p> 3768  * If the target VM is disconnected during the invoke (for example, through 3769  * the VirtualMachine dispose command) the method invocation continues. 3770  */ 3771  static class InvokeMethod { 3772  static final int COMMAND = 1; 4717  } 4718  } 4719  } 4720  } 4721  4722  /** 4723  * Invokes a instance method. 4724  * The method must be member of the object's type 4725  * or one of its superclasses, superinterfaces, or implemented interfaces. 4726  * Access control is not enforced; for example, private 4727  * methods can be invoked. 4728  * <p> 4729  * The method invocation will occur in the specified thread. 4730  * Method invocation can occur only if the specified thread 4731  * has been suspended by an event. 4732  * Method invocation is not supported 4733  * when the target VM has been suspended by the front-end. 4734  * <p> 4735  * The specified method is invoked with the arguments in the specified 4736  * argument list. 4737  * The method invocation is synchronous; the reply packet is not 4738  * sent until the invoked method returns in the target VM. 4739  * The return value (possibly the void value) is 4740  * included in the reply packet. 4741  * If the invoked method throws an exception, the 4742  * exception object ID is set in the reply packet; otherwise, the 4743  * exception object ID is null. 4744  * <p> 4745  * For primitive arguments, the argument value's type must match the 4746  * argument's type exactly. For object arguments, there must be a 4747  * widening reference conversion from the argument value's type to the 4748  * argument's type and the argument's type must be loaded. 4749  * <p> 4750  * By default, all threads in the target VM are resumed while 4751  * the method is being invoked if they were previously 4752  * suspended by an event or by a command. 4753  * This is done to prevent the deadlocks 4754  * that will occur if any of the threads own monitors 4755  * that will be needed by the invoked method. It is possible that 4756  * breakpoints or other events might occur during the invocation. 4757  * Note, however, that this implicit resume acts exactly like 4758  * the ThreadReference resume command, so if the thread's suspend 4759  * count is greater than 1, it will remain in a suspended state 4760  * during the invocation. By default, when the invocation completes, 4761  * all threads in the target VM are suspended, regardless their state 4762  * before the invocation. 4763  * <p> 4764  * The resumption of other threads during the invoke can be prevented 4765  * by specifying the INVOKE_SINGLE_THREADED 4766  * bit flag in the <code>options</code> field; however, 4767  * there is no protection against or recovery from the deadlocks 4768  * described above, so this option should be used with great caution. 4769  * Only the specified thread will be resumed (as described for all 4770  * threads above). Upon completion of a single threaded invoke, the invoking thread 4771  * will be suspended once again. Note that any threads started during 4772  * the single threaded invocation will not be suspended when the 4773  * invocation completes. 4774  * <p> 4775  * If the target VM is disconnected during the invoke (for example, through 4776  * the VirtualMachine dispose command) the method invocation continues. 4777  */ 4778  static class InvokeMethod { 4779  static final int COMMAND = 6; The called method is the current method (as 5932  * defined by the Frames section in 5933  * <cite>The Java&trade; Virtual Machine Specification</cite>) 5934  * for the specified thread at the time this command 5935  * is received. 5936  * <p> 5937  * The specified thread must be suspended. 5938  * The return occurs when execution of Java programming 5939  * language code is resumed on this thread. Between sending this 5940  * command and resumption of thread execution, the 5941  * state of the stack is undefined. 5942  * <p> 5943  * No further instructions are executed in the called 5944  * method. Specifically, finally blocks are not executed. Note: 5945  * this can cause inconsistent states in the application. 5946  * <p> 5947  * A lock acquired by calling the called method (if it is a 5948  * synchronized method) and locks acquired by entering 5949  * synchronized blocks within the called method are 5950  * released. Note: this does not apply to JNI locks or 5951  * java.util.concurrent.locks locks. 5952  * <p> 5953  * Events, such as MethodExit, are generated as they would be in 5954  * a normal return. 5955  * <p> 5956  * The called method must be a non-native Java programming 5957  * language method. 6485  private EventRequest() {} // hide constructor 6486  6487  /** 6488  * Set an event request. If none of those filters cause the event to be 6530  * suppressed, the event is reported. Otherwise, the event is not 6531  * reported. In either case subsequent events are never reported for 6532  * this request. 6533  * This modifier can be used with any event kind. 6534  */ 6535  static class Count extends ModifierCommon { 6536  static final byte ALT_ID = 1; 6537  static Modifier create(int count) { 6538  return new Modifier(ALT_ID, new Count(count)); 6539  } 6540  6541  /** 6542  * Count before event. 7573  } 7574  name = ps.readString(); 7575  if (vm.traceReceives) { 7576  vm.printReceiveTrace(4, "name(String): " + name); 7577  } 7578  } 7579  } 7580  7581  /** 7582  * Returns the class loader of this module. 7583  * <p>Since JDWP version 9. 7584  */ 7585  static class ClassLoader { 7586  static final int COMMAND = 2; 7587  7588  static ClassLoader process(VirtualMachineImpl vm, 7589  ModuleReferenceImpl module) 7590  throws JDWPException { 7591  PacketStream ps = enqueueCommand(vm, module); 7592  return waitForReply(vm, ps); 7593  } 7594  7595  static PacketStream enqueueCommand(VirtualMachineImpl vm, 7596  ModuleReferenceImpl module) { 7597  PacketStream ps = new PacketStream(vm, COMMAND_SET, COMMAND); 7598  if ((vm.traceFlags & VirtualMachineImpl.TRACE_SENDS) != 0) { 7599  vm.printTrace("Sending Command(id=" + ps.pkt.id + ") JDWP.ModuleReference.ClassLoader"+(ps.pkt.flags!=0?", FLAGS=" + ps.pkt.flags:"")); 7628  } 7629  } 7630  } 7631  } 7632  7633  static class Event { 7634  static final int COMMAND_SET = 64; 7635  private Event() {} // hide constructor 7636  7637  /** 7638  * Several events may occur at a given time in the target VM. 7639  * For example, there may be more than one breakpoint request 7640  * for a given location 7641  * or you might single step to the same location as a 7642  * breakpoint request. These events are delivered 7643  * together as a composite event. For uniformity, a 7644  * composite event is always used 7645  * to deliver events, even if there is only one event to report. 7646  * <P> 7647  * The events that are grouped in a composite event are restricted in the 7648  * following ways: 7649  * <UL> 7650  * <LI>Only with other thread start events for the same thread: 7651  * <UL> 7652  * <LI>Thread Start Event 7653  * </UL> 7654  * <LI>Only with other thread death events for the same thread: 7655  * <UL> 7656  * <LI>Thread Death Event 7657  * </UL> 7658  * <LI>Only with other class prepare events for the same class: 7659  * <UL> 7660  * <LI>Class Prepare Event 7661  * </UL> 7662  * <LI>Only with other class unload events for the same class: 7663  * <UL> 7664  * <LI>Class Unload Event 7665  * </UL> 7666  * <LI>Only with other access watchpoint events for the same field access: 7667  * <UL> 7668  * <LI>Access Watchpoint Event 7669  * </UL> 7670  * <LI>Only with other modification watchpoint events for the same field 7671  * modification: 7672  * <UL> 7673  * <LI>Modification Watchpoint Event 7674  * </UL> 7675  * <LI>Only with other Monitor contended enter events for the same monitor object: 7676  * <UL> 7677  * <LI>Monitor Contended Enter Event 7678  * </UL> 7679  * <LI>Only with other Monitor contended entered events for the same monitor object: 7680  * <UL> 7681  * <LI>Monitor Contended Entered Event 7682  * </UL> 7683  * <LI>Only with other Monitor wait events for the same monitor object: 7684  * <UL> 7685  * <LI>Monitor Wait Event 7686  * </UL> 7687  * <LI>Only with other Monitor waited events for the same monitor object: 7688  * <UL> 7689  * <LI>Monitor Waited Event 7690  * </UL> 7691  * <LI>Only with other ExceptionEvents for the same exception occurrance: 7692  * <UL> 7693  * <LI>ExceptionEvent 7694  * </UL> 7695  * <LI>Only with other members of this group, at the same location 7696  * and in the same thread: 7697  * <UL> 7698  * <LI>Breakpoint Event 7699  * <LI>Step Event 7700  * <LI>Method Entry Event 7701  * <LI>Method Exit Event 7702  * </UL> 7703  * </UL> 7704  * <P> 7705  * The VM Start Event and VM Death Event are automatically generated events. 7706  * This means they do not need to be requested using the 7707  * <a href="#JDWP_EventRequest_Set">EventRequest.Set</a> command. 7708  * The VM Start event signals the completion of VM initialization. The VM Death 7709  * event signals the termination of the VM. 7710  * If there is a debugger connected at the time when an automatically generated 7711  * event occurs it is sent from the target VM. Automatically generated events may 7712  * also be requested using the EventRequest.Set command and thus multiple events 7713  * of the same event kind will be sent from the target VM when an event occurs. 7714  * Automatically generated events are sent with the requestID field 7715  * in the Event Data set to 0. The value of the suspendPolicy field in the 7716  * Event Data depends on the event. For the automatically generated VM Start 7717  * Event the value of suspendPolicy is not defined and is therefore implementation 7718  * or configuration specific. In the Sun implementation, for example, the 7719  * suspendPolicy is specified as an option to the JDWP agent at launch-time. 7720  * The automatically generated VM Death Event will have the suspendPolicy set to 7721  * NONE. 7722  */ 7723  static class Composite { 7724  static final int COMMAND = 100; 7725  7726  static class Events { 7727  abstract static class EventsCommon { 7728  abstract byte eventKind(); 7729  } 7730  7731  /** 7732  * Event kind selector 7733  */ 7734  final byte eventKind; 7735  EventsCommon aEventsCommon; 7736  7737  Events(VirtualMachineImpl vm, PacketStream ps) { 7738  eventKind = ps.readByte(); 7739  if (vm.traceReceives) { 7740  vm.printReceiveTrace(5, "eventKind(byte): " + eventKind); 7741  } 7742  switch (eventKind) { 7743  case JDWP.EventKind.VM_START: 7744  aEventsCommon = new VMStart(vm, ps); 7745  break; 7746  case JDWP.EventKind.SINGLE_STEP: 7747  aEventsCommon = new SingleStep(vm, ps); 7748  break; 7749  case JDWP.EventKind.BREAKPOINT: 7750  aEventsCommon = new Breakpoint(vm, ps); 7751  break; 7752  case JDWP.EventKind.METHOD_ENTRY: 7753  aEventsCommon = new MethodEntry(vm, ps); 7754  break; 7755  case JDWP.EventKind.METHOD_EXIT: 7756  aEventsCommon = new MethodExit(vm, ps); 7757  break; 7758  case JDWP.EventKind.METHOD_EXIT_WITH_RETURN_VALUE: 7759  aEventsCommon = new MethodExitWithReturnValue(vm, ps); 7760  break; 7761  case JDWP.EventKind.MONITOR_CONTENDED_ENTER: 7762  aEventsCommon = new MonitorContendedEnter(vm, ps); 7763  break; 7764  case JDWP.EventKind.MONITOR_CONTENDED_ENTERED: 7765  aEventsCommon = new MonitorContendedEntered(vm, ps); 7766  break; 7767  case JDWP.EventKind.MONITOR_WAIT: 7768  aEventsCommon = new MonitorWait(vm, ps); 7769  break; 7770  case JDWP.EventKind.MONITOR_WAITED: 7771  aEventsCommon = new MonitorWaited(vm, ps); 7772  break; 7773  case JDWP.EventKind.EXCEPTION: 7774  aEventsCommon = new Exception(vm, ps); 7775  break; 7776  case JDWP.EventKind.THREAD_START: 7777  aEventsCommon = new ThreadStart(vm, ps); 7778  break; 7779  case JDWP.EventKind.THREAD_DEATH: 7780  aEventsCommon = new ThreadDeath(vm, ps); 7781  break; 7782  case JDWP.EventKind.CLASS_PREPARE: 7783  aEventsCommon = new ClassPrepare(vm, ps); 7784  break; 7785  case JDWP.EventKind.CLASS_UNLOAD: 7786  aEventsCommon = new ClassUnload(vm, ps); 7787  break; 7788  case JDWP.EventKind.FIELD_ACCESS: 7789  aEventsCommon = new FieldAccess(vm, ps); 7790  break; 7791  case JDWP.EventKind.FIELD_MODIFICATION: 7792  aEventsCommon = new FieldModification(vm, ps); 7793  break; 7794  case JDWP.EventKind.VM_DEATH: 7795  aEventsCommon = new VMDeath(vm, ps); 7796  break; 7797  } 7798  } 7799  7800  /** 7801  * Notification of initialization of a target VM. 8291  } 8292  } 8293  } 8294  8295  /** 8296  * Notification of an exception in the target VM. 8297  * If the exception is thrown from a non-native method, 8298  * the exception event is generated at the location where the 8299  * exception is thrown. 8300  * If the exception is thrown from a native method, the exception event 8301  * is generated at the first non-native location reached after the exception 8302  * is thrown. 8303  */ 8304  static class Exception extends EventsCommon { 8305  static final byte ALT_ID = JDWP.EventKind.EXCEPTION; 8306  byte eventKind() { 8307  return ALT_ID; 8308  } 8309  8310  /** 8311  * Request that generated event 8312  */ 8313  final int requestID; 8314  8315  /** 8316  * Thread with exception 8317  */ 8318  final ThreadReferenceImpl thread; 8319  8320  /** 8321  * Location of exception throw 8322  * (or first non-native location after throw if thrown from a native method) 8323  */ 8324  final Location location; 8325  8326  /** 8327  * Thrown exception 8328  */ 8329  final ObjectReferenceImpl exception; 8330  8331  /** 8332  * Location of catch, or 0 if not caught. An exception 8333  * is considered to be caught if, at the point of the throw, the 8334  * current location is dynamically enclosed in a try statement that 8335  * handles the exception. (See the JVM specification for details). 8336  * If there is such a try statement, the catch location is the 8337  * first location in the appropriate catch clause. 8338  * <p> 8339  * If there are native methods in the call stack at the time of the 8340  * exception, there are important restrictions to note about the 8341  * returned catch location. In such cases, 8342  * it is not possible to predict whether an exception will be handled 8343  * by some native method on the call stack. 8344  * Thus, it is possible that exceptions considered uncaught 8345  * here will, in fact, be handled by a native method and not cause 8346  * termination of the target VM. Furthermore, it cannot be assumed that the 8347  * catch location returned here will ever be reached by the throwing 8348  * thread. If there is 8349  * a native frame between the current location and the catch location, 8350  * the exception might be handled and cleared in that native method 8351  * instead. 8352  * <p> 8353  * Note that compilers can generate try-catch blocks in some cases 8354  * where they are not explicit in the source code; for example, 8355  * the code generated for <code>synchronized</code> and 8356  * <code>finally</code> blocks can contain implicit try-catch blocks. 8357  * If such an implicitly generated try-catch is 8358  * present on the call stack at the time of the throw, the exception 8359  * will be considered caught even though it appears to be uncaught from 8360  * examination of the source code. 8361  */ 8362  final Location catchLocation; 8363  8364  Exception(VirtualMachineImpl vm, PacketStream ps) { 8365  requestID = ps.readInt(); 8366  if (vm.traceReceives) { 8367  vm.printReceiveTrace(6, "requestID(int): " + requestID); 8368  } 8369  thread = ps.readThreadReference(); 8370  if (vm.traceReceives) { 8371  vm.printReceiveTrace(6, "thread(ThreadReferenceImpl): " + (thread==null?"NULL":"ref="+thread.ref())); 8372  } 8373  location = ps.readLocation(); 8374  if (vm.traceReceives) { 8375  vm.printReceiveTrace(6, "location(Location): " + location); 8376  } 8377  exception = ps.readTaggedObjectReference(); 8378  if (vm.traceReceives) { 8379  vm.printReceiveTrace(6, "exception(ObjectReferenceImpl): " + (exception==null?"NULL":"ref="+exception.ref())); 8380  } 8381  catchLocation = ps.readLocation(); 8382  if (vm.traceReceives) { 8383  vm.printReceiveTrace(6, "catchLocation(Location): " + catchLocation); 8384  } 8385  } 8386  } 8387  8388  /** 8389  * Notification of a new running thread in the target VM. 8390  * The new thread can be the result of a call to 8391  * <code>java.lang.Thread.start</code> or the result of 8392  * attaching a new thread to the VM though JNI. The 8393  * notification is generated by the new thread some time before 8394  * its execution starts. 8395  * Because of this timing, it is possible to receive other events 8396  * for the thread before this event is received.
